## üìã Project Context Files

### üåç Global CLAUDE.md

```markdown
- all scripts should be written assuming they are to be run from any directory. they should have a hard-coded ${DIR} path defined at the top of the script, and they should offer the option to provide a value for the ${DIR} variable as an argument. All paths in the program should be relative to the ${DIR} variable.
- all functions should use vimfolds to collapse functionality. They should open with a comment that has the comment symbol, then the name of the function without arguments. On the next line, the function should be defined with arguments. Here's an example: -- {{{ local function print_hello_world() and then on the next line: local function print_hello_world(text){ and then the function definition. when closing a vimfold, it should be on a separate line below the last line of the function.
- to create a project, mkdir docs notes src libs assets
- to initialize a project, read the vision document located in prj-dir/notes/vision - then create documentation related to it in prj-dir/docs/ - then repeat, then repeat. Ensure there is a roadmap document split into phases. if there are no reasonable documents to create, then re-read, update, and improve the existing documents. Then, break the roadmap file into issues, starting with the prj-dir/issues/phase-1/ directory. be as specific as need be. ensure that issues are created with these protocols: name: ID-descr where ID is the sequential ID number of the issue problem idea ticket, and descr is a dash-separated short one-sentence description of the issue. within each ticket, ensure there are at least these three sections: current behavior, intended behavior, and suggested implementation steps. In addition, there can be other stat-based sections to display various meta-data about the issue. There may also be a related documents or tools section. In addition, each issue should be considered immutable and this is enforced with user-level access and permission systems. It is necessary to preserve consent of access to imagination. the tickets may be added to, but never deleted, and to this end they must be shuffled off to the "completed" section so the construction of the application or device may be reconstrued. Ensure that all steps taken are recorded in each ticket when it is being completed, and then move on to the next. At each phase, a test-program should be created / updated-with-entirely-new-content which displays the progress of the program. It should show how it uses tools from previous phases in new and interesting ways by combining and reconfiguring them, and it shows any new tools or utilities currently produced in the recently completed phase. This test program should be runnable with a simple bash script, and it should live in the issues/completed/phase-X/ directory, where X is the number of the phase of the project's lifecycle. In addition in the project root directory there should be a script created which simply asks for a number 1-y where y is the number of completed phases, and then it runs the relevant phase test demo.
- bash commands or scripts that can be called from the command line should have a flag -I which runs the script in interactive mode. Meaning, the commands will be built by querying the user for each category of possible flag. Ideally, few flag categories, many flag options within each category.
- all interactive modes should allow for index based selection of options in addition to arrow-key and vim-keybinding navigation. (i is select in vim mode, also shift+A)
- for every implemented change to the project, there must always be an issue file. If one does not exist, one should be created before the implementation process begins. In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

### üîÆ Vision: notes/vision

```
# RISC-V University Vision

## Project Overview
RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.

## Core Mission
To democratize computer architecture education by providing accessible, comprehensive, and engaging learning materials for RISC-V instruction set architecture.

## Target Audience
- Computer science students
- Software engineers learning low-level programming
- Educators teaching computer architecture
- Hobbyists interested in processor design

## Key Features
- Interactive RISC-V assembly tutorials
- Virtual RISC-V processor simulator
- Step-by-step instruction execution visualization
- Progressive difficulty levels from basic to advanced
- Real-time code compilation and execution
- Performance analysis tools
- Educational resources and reference materials

## Success Metrics
- User engagement and completion rates
- Learning outcome assessments
- Community contributions and feedback
- Platform adoption in educational institutions

## Long-term Vision
Create the premier online destination for RISC-V education, fostering a community of learners and educators while advancing understanding of computer architecture fundamentals.
```

### üîÆ Vision: vision

```
I decided to learn risc-v assembly, and this is the university playground made.

each of the directories in /home/ritz/programming/ai-stuff/ contain a sample
project, all of them incomplete, and all of them serving as examples of the
design and philosophy of the example projects built for university.

All in risc-v assembly.

there are many documents and vision statements, and many of them are useful.
the source-code is always broken, to give the student room to explore.
and none of it is in risc-v assembly.
that is reserved for this directory, the risc-v-university-playground.

in this directory, we start by creating lesson plans. we do this after reviewing
the tickets of suggested or intended next-steps for learning the systems.

future phases should include all the concepts discussed in previous ones,
making up side-quests and similar-objectives which use the previous functionality
in the new and revising current subject.

the ordering of the syllabus matters, but it's vague and broken down by chapter
so there's plenty of room to expand. in fact, each chapter gets it's own
directory, with several .md files that explain a particular concept. ideally,
with examples, or picture diagrams which illustrate a point. these can be
constructed with code that produces arrow diagrams pointing at variables which
represent various concepts and which have x,y positions and are arranged
in a map pseudo-randomly according to theme as determined by an LLM embedding
which can be found in one or more of the directories above.

the issues in this project include all work items that may be completed while
building the project. No ticket, no work is done. everything must be written
down, captured somewhere, ideally in the relevant ticket but sometimes in
related and assorted documentation. Ideally, this documentation would be
referenced in the ticket as well, with information appended but not edited.

the examples can start out simple. they should grow in complexity as the users
toolkit is created and expanded. new ideas and new concepts should emerge, as
the user creates tickets and the build-out of capabilities is un-depleted.

a description of each inspirational example project (none of which are editable)
should be included in the docs directory, in a subdirectory called examples.
these examples should have lists of required functionality (functions and data-
-structures and cyclical operations (services)) that are required for that
example but which are not present in the "recently-explained-functionalities.md"
file.

each vision file should be mentioned in a summary that includes the most unique
keys or related descriptors for each vision file, so it may be easily found
when being examined by data.

in general, files that feel important or shallow should be examined and updated
more than once in the same or different contexts. Often it makes sense to read
in one file, write and update it with what's earlier in context, then read a 
different file, then update the first one again. other times it makes sense to
read in a file, update it, then read in a nother file, then combine both and
create a new one and remove both old files. There are many designs patterns to
find, see if you can collect them all!

special attention and care should be taken to explaining the non-algorithmic
features and considerations of risc-v. each consideration or feature should have
a lesson oriented around it, with an emphasis on exploring new topics and not on
routine or exercise. there must always be luck involved - let the player user
take the next step.
```

```

# RISC-V University Vision

## Project Overview
RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.

## Core Mission
To democratize computer architecture education by providing accessible, comprehensive, and engaging learning materials for RISC-V instruction set architecture.

## Target Audience
- Computer science students
- Software engineers learning low-level programming
- Educators teaching computer architecture
- Hobbyists interested in processor design

## Key Features
- Interactive RISC-V assembly tutorials
- Virtual RISC-V processor simulator
- Step-by-step instruction execution visualization
- Progressive difficulty levels from basic to advanced
- Real-time code compilation and execution
- Performance analysis tools
- Educational resources and reference materials

## Success Metrics
- User engagement and completion rates
- Learning outcome assessments
- Community contributions and feedback
- Platform adoption in educational institutions

## Long-term Vision
Create the premier online destination for RISC-V education, fostering a community of learners and educators while advancing understanding of computer architecture fundamentals.
```

## üìã Project Context Files

### üåç Global CLAUDE.md

```markdown
- all scripts should be written assuming they are to be run from any directory. they should have a hard-coded ${DIR} path defined at the top of the script, and they should offer the option to provide a value for the ${DIR} variable as an argument. Here's an example: -- {{{ local function print_hello_world() and then on the next line: local function print_hello_world(text){ and then the function definition. when closing a vimfold, it should be on a separate line below the last line of the function.
- to create a project, mkdir docs notes src libs assets
- to initialize a project, read the vision document located in prj-dir/notes/vision - then create documentation related to it in prj-dir/docs/ - then repeat, then repeat. Ensure there is a roadmap document split into phases. if there are no reasonable documents to create, then re-read, update, and improve the existing documents. Then, break the roadmap file into issues, starting with the prj-dir/issues/phase-1/ directory. be as specific as need be. ensure that issues are created with these protocols: name: ID-descr where ID is the sequential ID number of the issue problem idea ticket, and descr is a dash-separated short one-sentence description of the issue. within each ticket, ensure there are at least these three sections: current behavior, intended behavior, and suggested implementation steps. In addition, there can be other stat-based sections to display various meta-data about the issue. There may also be a related documents or tools section. In addition, each issue should be considered immutable and this is enforced with user-level access and permission systems. It is necessary to preserve consent of access to imagination. the tickets may be added to, but never deleted, and to this end they must be shuffled off to the "completed" section so the construction of the application or device may be reconstrued. Ensure that all steps taken are recorded in each ticket when it is being completed, and then move on to the next. At each phase, a test-program should be created / updated-with-entirely-new-content which displays the progress of the program. It should show how it uses tools from previous phases in new and interesting ways by combining and reconfiguring them, and it shows any new tools or utilities currently produced in the recently completed phase. This test program should be runnable with a simple bash script, and it should live in the issues/completed/phase-X/ directory, where X is the number of the phase of the project's lifecycle. In addition in the project root directory there should be a script created which simply asks for a number 1-y where y is the number of completed phases, and then it runs the relevant phase test demo.
- bash commands or scripts that can be called from the command line should have a flag -I which runs the script in interactive mode. Meaning, the commands will be built by querying the user for each category of possible flag. Ideally, few flag categories, many flag options within each category.
- all interactive modes should allow for index based selection of options in addition to arrow-key and vim-keybinding navigation. (i is select in vim mode, also shift+A)
- for every implemented change to the project, there must always be an issue file. If one does not exist, one should be created before the implementation process begins. In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

### üîÆ Vision: notes/vision

```
# RISC-V University Vision

## Project Overview
RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.

## Core Mission
To democratize computer architecture education by providing accessible, comprehensive, and engaging learning materials for RISC-V instruction set architecture.

## Target Audience
- Computer science students
- Software engineers learning low-level programming
- Educators teaching computer architecture
- Hobbyists interested in processor design

## Key Features
- Interactive RISC-V assembly tutorials
- Virtual RISC-V processor simulator
- Step-by-step instruction execution visualization
- Progressive difficulty levels from basic to advanced
- Real-time code compilation and execution
- Performance analysis tools
- Educational resources and reference materials

## Success Metrics
- User engagement and completion rates
- Learning outcome assessments
- Community contributions and feedback
- Platform adoption in educational institutions

## Long-term Vision
Create the premier online destination for RISC-V education, fostering a community of learners and educators while advancing understanding of computer architecture fundamentals.
```

### üîÆ Vision: vision

```
I decided to learn risc-v assembly, and this is the university playground made.

each of the directories in /home/ritz/programming/ai-stuff/ contain a sample
project, all of them incomplete, and all of them serving as examples of the
design and philosophy of the example projects built for university.

All in risc-v assembly.

there are many documents and vision statements, and many of them are useful.
the source-code is always broken, to give the student room to explore.
and none of it is in risc-v assembly.
that is reserved for this directory, the risc-v-university-playground.

in this directory, we start by creating lesson plans. we do this after reviewing
the tickets of suggested or intended next-steps for learning the systems.

future phases should include all the concepts discussed in previous ones,
making up side-quests and similar-objectives which use the previous functionality
in the new and revising current subject.

the ordering of the syllabus matters, but it's vague and broken down by chapter
so there's plenty of room to expand. in fact, each chapter gets it's own
directory, with several .md files that explain a particular concept. ideally,
with examples, or picture diagrams which illustrate a point. these can be
constructed with code that produces arrow diagrams pointing at variables which
represent various concepts and which have x,y positions and are arranged
in a map pseudo-randomly according to theme as determined by an LLM embedding
which can be found in one or more of the directories above.

the issues in this project include all work items that may be completed while
building the project. No ticket, no work is done. everything must be written
down, captured somewhere, ideally in the relevant ticket but sometimes in
related and assorted documentation. Ideally, this documentation would be
referenced in the ticket as well, with information appended but not edited.

the examples can start out simple. they should grow in complexity as the users
toolkit is created and expanded. new ideas and new concepts should emerge, as
the user creates tickets and the build-out of capabilities is un-depleted.

a description of each inspirational example project (none of which are editable)
should be included in the docs directory, in a subdirectory called examples.
these examples should have lists of required functionality (functions and data-
-structures and cyclical operations (services)) that are required for that
example but which are not present in the "recently-explained-functionalities.md"
file.

each vision file should be mentioned in a summary that includes the most unique
keys or related descriptors for each vision file, so it may be easily found
when being examined by data.

in general, files that feel important or shallow should be examined and updated
more than once in the same or different contexts. Often it makes sense to read
in one file, write and update it with what's earlier in context, then read a 
different file, then update the first one again. other times it makes sense to
read in a file, update it, then read in a nother file, then combine both and
create a new one and remove both old files. There are many designs patterns to
find, see if you can collect them all!

special attention and care should be taken to explaining the non-algorithmic
features and considerations of risc-v. each consideration or feature should have
a lesson oriented around it, with an emphasis on exploring new topics and not on
routine or exercise. there must always be luck involved - let the player user
take the next step.

```

## üìã Project Context Files

### üåç Global CLAUDE.md

```markdown
- all scripts should be written assuming they are to be run from any directory. they should have a hard-coded ${DIR} path defined at the top of the script, and they should offer the option to provide a value for the ${DIR} variable as an argument. All paths in the program should be relative to the ${DIR} variable.
- all functions should use vimfolds to collapse functionality. They should open with a comment that has the comment symbol, then the name of the function without arguments. On the next line, the function should be defined with arguments. Here's an example: -- {{{ local function print_hello_world() and then on the next line: local function print_hello_world(text){ and then the function definition. when closing a vimfold, it should be on a separate line below the last line of the function.
- to create a project, mkdir docs notes src libs assets
- to initialize a project, read the vision document located in prj-dir/notes/vision - then create documentation related to it in prj-dir/docs/ - then repeat, then repeat. Ensure there is a roadmap document split into phases. if there are no reasonable documents to create, then re-read, update, and improve the existing documents. Then, break the roadmap file into issues, starting with the prj-dir/issues/phase-1/ directory. be as specific as need be. ensure that issues are created with these protocols: name: ID-descr where ID is the sequential ID number of the issue problem idea ticket, and descr is a dash-separated short one-sentence description of the issue. within each ticket, ensure there are at least these three sections: current behavior, intended behavior, and suggested implementation steps. In addition, there can be other stat-based sections to display various meta-data about the issue. There may also be a related documents or tools section. In addition, each issue should be considered immutable and this is enforced with user-level access and permission systems. It is necessary to preserve consent of access to imagination. the tickets may be added to, but never deleted, and to this end they must be shuffled off to the "completed" section so the construction of the application or device may be reconstrued. Ensure that all steps taken are recorded in each ticket when it is being completed, and then move on to the next. At each phase, a test-program should be created / updated-with-entirely-new-content which displays the progress of the program. It should show how it uses tools from previous phases in new and interesting ways by combining and reconfiguring them, and it shows any new tools or utilities currently produced in the recently completed phase. This test program should be runnable with a simple bash script, and it should live in the issues/completed/phase-X/ directory, where X is the number of the phase of the project's lifecycle. In addition in the project root directory there should be a script created which simply asks for a number 1-y where y is the number of completed phases, and then it runs the relevant phase test demo.
- bash commands or scripts that can be called from the command line should have a flag -I which runs the script in interactive mode. Meaning, the commands will be built by querying the user for each category of possible flag. Ideally, few flag categories, many flag options within each category.
- all interactive modes should allow for index based selection of options in addition to arrow-key and vim-keybinding navigation. (i is select in vim mode, also shift+A)
- for every implemented change to the project, there must always be an issue file. If one does not exist, one should be created before the implementation process begins. In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

## üìú Conversation 4: v4-complete.md

*File size: 39786 bytes*

**Generated:** 2025-11-06 02:22:08  
**Total Conversations:** 4  
**Ready for Distribution:** As the traveller pleases ‚ú®

## üìã Project Context Files

### üåç Global CLAUDE.md

```markdown
- all scripts should be written assuming they are to be run from any directory. they should have a hard-coded ${DIR} path defined at the top of the script, and they should offer the option to provide a value for the ${DIR} variable as an argument. All paths in the program should be relative to the ${DIR} variable.
- all functions should use vimfolds to collapse functionality. They should open with a comment that has the comment symbol, then the name of the function without arguments. On the next line, the function should be defined with arguments. Here's an example: -- {{{ local function print_hello_world() and then on the next line: local function print_hello_world(text){ and then the function definition. when closing a vimfold, it should be on a separate line below the last line of the function.
- to create a project, mkdir docs notes src libs assets
- to initialize a project, read the vision document located in prj-dir/notes/vision - then create documentation related to it in prj-dir/docs/ - then repeat, then repeat. Ensure there is a roadmap document split into phases. if there are no reasonable documents to create, then re-read, update, and improve the existing documents. Then, break the roadmap file into issues, starting with the prj-dir/issues/phase-1/ directory. be as specific as need be. ensure that issues are created with these protocols: name: ID-descr where ID is the sequential ID number of the issue problem idea ticket, and descr is a dash-separated short one-sentence description of the issue. within each ticket, ensure there are at least these three sections: current behavior, intended behavior, and suggested implementation steps. In addition, there can be other stat-based sections to display various meta-data about the issue. There may also be a related documents or tools section. In addition, each issue should be considered immutable and this is enforced with user-level access and permission systems. It is necessary to preserve consent of access to imagination. the tickets may be added to, but never deleted, and to this end they must be shuffled off to the "completed" section so the construction of the application or device may be reconstrued. Ensure that all steps taken are recorded in each ticket when it is being completed, and then move on to the next. At each phase, a test-program should be created / updated-with-entirely-new-content which displays the progress of the program. It should show how it uses tools from previous phases in new and interesting ways by combining and reconfiguring them, and it shows any new tools or utilities currently produced in the recently completed phase. This test program should be runnable with a simple bash script, and it should live in the issues/completed/phase-X/ directory, where X is the number of the phase of the project's lifecycle. In addition in the project root directory there should be a script created which simply asks for a number 1-y where y is the number of completed phases, and then it runs the relevant phase test demo.
- bash commands or scripts that can be called from the command line should have a flag -I which runs the script in interactive mode. Meaning, the commands will be built by querying the user for each category of possible flag. Ideally, few flag categories, many flag options within each category.
- all interactive modes should allow for index based selection of options in addition to arrow-key and vim-keybinding navigation. (i is select in vim mode, also shift+A)
- for every implemented change to the project, there must always be an issue file. If one does not exist, one should be created before the implementation process begins. In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

### üîÆ Vision: notes/vision

```
# RISC-V University Vision

## Project Overview
RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.

## Core Mission
To democratize computer architecture education by providing accessible, comprehensive, and engaging learning materials for RISC-V instruction set architecture.

## Target Audience
- Computer science students
- Software engineers learning low-level programming
- Educators teaching computer architecture
- Hobbyists interested in processor design

## Key Features
- Interactive RISC-V assembly tutorials
- Virtual RISC-V processor simulator
- Step-by-step instruction execution visualization
- Progressive difficulty levels from basic to advanced
- Real-time code compilation and execution
- Performance analysis tools
- Educational resources and reference materials

## Success Metrics
- User engagement and completion rates
- Learning outcome assessments
- Community contributions and feedback
- Platform adoption in educational institutions

## Long-term Vision
Create the premier online destination for RISC-V education, fostering a community of learners and educators while advancing understanding of computer architecture fundamentals.
```

### üîÆ Vision: vision

```
I decided to learn risc-v assembly, and this is the university playground made.

each of the directories in /home/ritz/programming/ai-stuff/ contain a sample
project, all of them incomplete, and all of them serving as examples of the
design and philosophy of the example projects built for university.

All in risc-v assembly.

there are many documents and vision statements, and many of them are useful.
the source-code is always broken, to give the student room to explore.
and none of it is in risc-v assembly.
that is reserved for this directory, the risc-v-university-playground.

in this directory, we start by creating lesson plans. we do this after reviewing
the tickets of suggested or intended next-steps for learning the systems.

future phases should include all the concepts discussed in previous ones,
making up side-quests and similar-objectives which use the previous functionality
in the new and revising current subject.

the ordering of the syllabus matters, but it's vague and broken down by chapter
so there's plenty of room to expand. in fact, each chapter gets it's own
directory, with several .md files that explain a particular concept. ideally,
with examples, or picture diagrams which illustrate a point. these can be
constructed with code that produces arrow diagrams pointing at variables which
represent various concepts and which have x,y positions and are arranged
in a map pseudo-randomly according to theme as determined by an LLM embedding
which can be found in one or more of the directories above.

the issues in this project include all work items that may be completed while
building the project. No ticket, no work is done. everything must be written
down, captured somewhere, ideally in the relevant ticket but sometimes in
related and assorted documentation. Ideally, this documentation would be
referenced in the ticket as well, with information appended but not edited.

the examples can start out simple. they should grow in complexity as the users
toolkit is created and expanded. new ideas and new concepts should emerge, as
the user creates tickets and the build-out of capabilities is un-depleted.

a description of each inspirational example project (none of which are editable)
should be included in the docs directory, in a subdirectory called examples.
these examples should have lists of required functionality (functions and data-
-structures and cyclical operations (services)) that are required for that
example but which are not present in the "recently-explained-functionalities.md"
file.

each vision file should be mentioned in a summary that includes the most unique
keys or related descriptors for each vision file, so it may be easily found
when being examined by data.

in general, files that feel important or shallow should be examined and updated
more than once in the same or different contexts. Often it makes sense to read
in one file, write and update it with what's earlier in context, then read a 
different file, then update the first one again. other times it makes sense to
read in a file, update it, then read in a nother file, then combine both and
create a new one and remove both old files. There are many designs patterns to
find, see if you can collect them all!

special attention and care should be taken to explaining the non-algorithmic
features and considerations of risc-v. each consideration or feature should have
a lesson oriented around it, with an emphasis on exploring new topics and not on
routine or exercise. there must always be luck involved - let the player user
take the next step.

```

In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
```markdown
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

### üîÆ Vision: notes/vision

```
# RISC-V University Vision

## Project Overview
RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.

## Core Mission
To democratize computer architecture education by providing accessible, comprehensive, and engaging learning materials for RISC-V instruction set architecture.

## Target Audience
- Computer science students
- Software engineers learning low-level programming
- Educators teaching computer architecture
- Hobbyists interested in processor design

## Key Features
- Interactive RISC-V assembly tutorials
- Virtual RISC-V processor simulator
- Step-by-step instruction execution visualization
- Progressive difficulty levels from basic to advanced
- Real-time code compilation and execution
- Performance analysis tools
- Educational resources and reference materials

## Success Metrics
- User engagement and completion rates
- Learning outcome assessments
- Community contributions and feedback
- Platform adoption in educational institutions

## Long-term Vision
Create the premier online destination for RISC-V education, fostering a community of learners and educators while advancing understanding of computer architecture fundamentals.
```

### üîÆ Vision: vision

```
I decided to learn risc-v assembly, and this is the university playground made.

each of the directories in /home/ritz/programming/ai-stuff/ contain a sample
project, all of them incomplete, and all of them serving as examples of the
design and philosophy of the example projects built for university.

All in risc-v assembly.

there are many documents and vision statements, and many of them are useful.
the source-code is always broken, to give the student room to explore.
and none of it is in risc-v assembly.
that is reserved for this directory, the risc-v-university-playground.

in this directory, we start by creating lesson plans. we do this after reviewing
the tickets of suggested or intended next-steps for learning the systems.

future phases should include all the concepts discussed in previous ones,
making up side-quests and similar-objectives which use the previous functionality
in the new and revising current subject.

the ordering of the syllabus matters, but it's vague and broken down by chapter
so there's plenty of room to expand. in fact, each chapter gets it's own
directory, with several .md files that explain a particular concept. ideally,
with examples, or picture diagrams which illustrate a point. these can be
constructed with code that produces arrow diagrams pointing at variables which
represent various concepts and which have x,y positions and are arranged
in a map pseudo-randomly according to theme as determined by an LLM embedding
which can be found in one or more of the directories above.

the issues in this project include all work items that may be completed while
building the project. No ticket, no work is done. everything must be written
down, captured somewhere, ideally in the relevant ticket but sometimes in
related and assorted documentation. Ideally, this documentation would be
referenced in the ticket as well, with information appended but not edited.

the examples can start out simple. they should grow in complexity as the users
toolkit is created and expanded. new ideas and new concepts should emerge, as
the user creates tickets and the build-out of capabilities is un-depleted.

a description of each inspirational example project (none of which are editable)
should be included in the docs directory, in a subdirectory called examples.
these examples should have lists of required functionality (functions and data-
-structures and cyclical operations (services)) that are required for that
example but which are not present in the "recently-explained-functionalities.md"
file.

each vision file should be mentioned in a summary that includes the most unique
keys or related descriptors for each vision file, so it may be easily found
when being examined by data.

in general, files that feel important or shallow should be examined and updated
more than once in the same or different contexts. Often it makes sense to read
in one file, write and update it with what's earlier in context, then read a 
different file, then update the first one again. other times it makes sense to
read in a file, update it, then read in a nother file, then combine both and
create a new one and remove both old files. There are many designs patterns to
find, see if you can collect them all!

special attention and care should be taken to explaining the non-algorithmic
features and considerations of risc-v. each consideration or feature should have
a lesson oriented around it, with an emphasis on exploring new topics and not on
routine or exercise. there must always be luck involved - let the player user
take the next step.

```

## üìã Project Context Files

### üåç Global CLAUDE.md

```markdown
- all scripts should be written assuming they are to be run from any directory. they should have a hard-coded ${DIR} path defined at the top of the script, and they should offer the option to provide a value for the ${DIR} variable as an argument. All paths in the program should be relative to the ${DIR} variable.
- all functions should use vimfolds to collapse functionality. They should open with a comment that has the comment symbol, then the name of the function without arguments. On the next line, the function should be defined with arguments. Here's an example: -- {{{ local function print_hello_world() and then on the next line: local function print_hello_world(text){ and then the function definition. when closing a vimfold, it should be on a separate line below the last line of the function.
- to create a project, mkdir docs notes src libs assets
- to initialize a project, read the vision document located in prj-dir/notes/vision - then create documentation related to it in prj-dir/docs/ - then repeat, then repeat. Ensure there is a roadmap document split into phases. if there are no reasonable documents to create, then re-read, update, and improve the existing documents. Then, break the roadmap file into issues, starting with the prj-dir/issues/phase-1/ directory. be as specific as need be. ensure that issues are created with these protocols: name: ID-descr where ID is the sequential ID number of the issue problem idea ticket, and descr is a dash-separated short one-sentence description of the issue. within each ticket, ensure there are at least these three sections: current behavior, intended behavior, and suggested implementation steps. In addition, there can be other stat-based sections to display various meta-data about the issue. There may also be a related documents or tools section. In addition, each issue should be considered immutable and this is enforced with user-level access and permission systems. It is necessary to preserve consent of access to imagination. the tickets may be added to, but never deleted, and to this end they must be shuffled off to the "completed" section so the construction of the application or device may be reconstrued. Ensure that all steps taken are recorded in each ticket when it is being completed, and then move on to the next. At each phase, a test-program should be created / updated-with-entirely-new-content which displays the progress of the program. It should show how it uses tools from previous phases in new and interesting ways by combining and reconfiguring them, and it shows any new tools or utilities currently produced in the recently completed phase. This test program should be runnable with a simple bash script, and it should live in the issues/completed/phase-X/ directory, where X is the number of the phase of the project's lifecycle. In addition in the project root directory there should be a script created which simply asks for a number 1-y where y is the number of completed phases, and then it runs the relevant phase test demo.
- bash commands or scripts that can be called from the command line should have a flag -I which runs the script in interactive mode. Meaning, the commands will be built by querying the user for each category of possible flag. Ideally, few flag categories, many flag options within each category.
- all interactive modes should allow for index based selection of options in addition to arrow-key and vim-keybinding navigation. (i is select in vim mode, also shift+A)
- for every implemented change to the project, there must always be an issue file. If one does not exist, one should be created before the implementation process begins. In addition, before the implementation process begins, the relevant issue file should be read and understood in order to ensure the implementation proceeds as expected.
- prefer error messages and breaking functionality over fallbacks. Be sure to query the user every time a fallback is used.
```

```
# RISC-V University Vision

RISC-V University is an educational platform designed to teach RISC-V architecture, assembly programming, and computer systems fundamentals through interactive learning modules and hands-on exercises.
```

‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ Written File: PROJECT_OVERVIEW.md (2877 bytes, 62 lines) ‚îÇ
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
‚îÇ   1 ‚îÇ # Preschool Ascension                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   2 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   3 ‚îÇ ## Project Overview                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   4 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   5 ‚îÇ **Alternative Titles:** preschool-dimension, preschool-time-potty-out, potty-potty-playground ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   6 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   7 ‚îÇ Preschool Ascension is an interactive game designed for the ABDL (Adult Baby Diaper Lover) community. The game combines adventure, puzzle-solving, and LLM-powered interactions in a unique dimensional setting. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   8 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   9 ‚îÇ ## Core Concept                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  10 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  11 ‚îÇ Players take on the role of adults who have been transported from their regular world (heaven) through a portal into the "preschool dimension" - a halfway point between heaven and hell. The goal is to navigate this dimension and find a way back to the regular world. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  12 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ ## Game World                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  14 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ ### The Preschool Environment                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  16 ‚îÇ - **Main Building**: Large brick and mortar structure with safety-focused design ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  17 ‚îÇ - **Interior**: Walls covered with dense, layered cushions creating bouncy, mattress-like surfaces ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  18 ‚îÇ - **Flooring**: Gym-mat density with t-shirt material covering for safety ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  19 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  20 ‚îÇ ### The Endless Basement                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  21 ‚îÇ - Primary game environment with both indoor and outdoor areas ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  22 ‚îÇ - Secret train system provides access to satellite-unreachable locations ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  23 ‚îÇ - Dangerous amphibian and dinosaur creatures inhabit the wilderness areas ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ ## Gameplay Mechanics                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ ### Core Systems                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ 1. **Accident Management**: Players must avoid accidents on floors to prevent attracting monsters ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ 2. **LLM-Powered NPCs**: Spirit creatures and monsters are controlled by local LLM with conversation-based resolution ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  30 ‚îÇ 3. **Climbing/Traversal**: 3rd-person climbing mechanics using dual-stick controls ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ 4. **Material Analysis**: Detailed examination system for all in-game objects ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ ### Control Scheme                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  34 ‚îÇ - **Left/Right Sticks**: Arm control for climbing and aiming ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ - **D-Pad**: Movement and strafing                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  36 ‚îÇ - **Face Buttons**: Four different jump types        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  37 ‚îÇ - **Bumpers**: Camera rotation                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  38 ‚îÇ - **Triggers**: Character rotation                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  39 ‚îÇ - **Back Buttons (1-4)**: Customizable interaction buttons for hands, talking, and object examination ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  40 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  41 ‚îÇ ### NPC Interactions                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  42 ‚îÇ - **Consent-Based Combat**: No traditional damage system ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  43 ‚îÇ - **Conversation Resolution**: Players must convince hostile entities through dialogue ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  44 ‚îÇ - **Learning AI**: NPCs learn about consent through non-violent interactions ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  45 ‚îÇ - **Multiple Choice Options**: Text-based options with potential animations and visual feedback ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  46 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  47 ‚îÇ ## Technical Features                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  48 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  49 ‚îÇ ### LLM Integration                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  50 ‚îÇ - Local LLM for NPC behavior and dialogue            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  51 ‚îÇ - Context-aware conversation trees                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  52 ‚îÇ - Serializable text-based option generation          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  53 ‚îÇ - Environmental modification capabilities            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  54 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  55 ‚îÇ ### Material System                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  56 ‚îÇ - Detailed component analysis for all objects        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  57 ‚îÇ - Weight, density, and material properties           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  58 ‚îÇ - Visual blueprint generation                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  59 ‚îÇ - Infinite context storage with ROM-based persistence ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  60 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  61 ‚îÇ ## Development Goals                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  62 ‚îÇ                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  63 ‚îÇ The game aims to create a safe, educational environment that explores themes of consent, communication, and problem-solving within a fantastical setting designed specifically for the ABDL community. ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
‚îÇ   1 ‚îÇ # Claude Project Instructions               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   2 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   3 ‚îÇ ## Git Repository Management                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   4 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   5 ‚îÇ **CRITICAL**: For every change made to this project, you MUST update the git repository to ensure no information is lost. This includes: ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   6 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   7 ‚îÇ - All code changes and modifications        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   8 ‚îÇ - Directory structure changes               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   9 ‚îÇ - Documentation updates                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  10 ‚îÇ - Configuration file changes                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  11 ‚îÇ - Any notes or advancement made during development ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  12 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ **Exceptions**: Do not commit build artifacts that are automatically generated and can be deterministically recreated. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  14 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ ## State Management                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  16 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  17 ‚îÇ For complex computational interface changes that require LLM behavior modifications, create a storage system that maintains every state of the machine in a compressible, git-style format. This should operate on parallel branches for different computational interface matrices. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  18 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  19 ‚îÇ ## Variable Naming Convention               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  20 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  21 ‚îÇ - Use `${DIR}` instead of `${PROJECT_ROOT}` for easier typing and consistency ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  22 ‚îÇ - All scripts should be written to run from any directory with a hard-coded `${DIR}` path ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  23 ‚îÇ - Scripts should accept `${DIR}` as an optional argument override ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ ## Development Workflow                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ 1. Make any necessary changes               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ 2. Stage all relevant files: `git add .`    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ 3. Commit with descriptive message: `git commit -m "Description of changes"` ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  30 ‚îÇ 4. Continue development                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ This ensures a complete history of all project evolution and prevents data loss during development. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  34 ‚îÇ ## Unity Development Guidelines             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  36 ‚îÇ ### Debug Output Strategy                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  37 ‚îÇ - Debug information should be written to files for LLM analysis, NOT console ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  38 ‚îÇ - Console should only show developer-focused messages like: ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  39 ‚îÇ   - "This is where we could expand functionality" ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  40 ‚îÇ   - "What if this part worked differently? Please write a vision document" ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  41 ‚îÇ   - "Past behavior recordings available in directory: X" ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  42 ‚îÇ - Use DebugLogger.Instance for file-based logging with categories ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  43 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  44 ‚îÇ ### Testing Workflow                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  45 ‚îÇ - User pushes Play button in Unity Editor   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  46 ‚îÇ - User describes test results and observations ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  47 ‚îÇ - Debug logs are automatically written to files for LLM review ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  48 ‚îÇ - LLM can analyze patterns and suggest improvements ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  49 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  50 ‚îÇ ### Unity Project Structure                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  51 ‚îÇ - Follow the established Assets/ organization ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  52 ‚îÇ - All external dependencies built from source in /external-libraries/ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  53 ‚îÇ - Configuration system handles all game settings ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  54 ‚îÇ - Event bus for decoupled communication between systems ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  55 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  56 ‚îÇ ## Issue Management System                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  57 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  58 ‚îÇ ### Issue File Structure                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  59 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  60 ‚îÇ Issues are stored in the `/issues/` directory within the project. Each issue is a standalone `.issue` file that can be easily read and managed. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  61 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  62 ‚îÇ ### File Naming Convention                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  63 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  64 ‚îÇ Issues follow this naming pattern: `{ID}-{description}.issue` ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  65 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  66 ‚îÇ - **ID**: Sequential number that provides guidance toward project progress ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  67 ‚îÇ - **description**: Short, one-sentence description of the issue ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  68 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  69 ‚îÇ Example: `001-implement-basic-player-movement.issue` ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  70 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  71 ‚îÇ ### Issue File Format                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  72 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  73 ‚îÇ Each `.issue` file must contain the following sections: ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  74 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  75 ‚îÇ ```                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  76 ‚îÇ # Issue {ID}: {Title}                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  77 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  78 ‚îÇ ## Current Behavior                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  79 ‚îÇ Description of what currently happens or exists. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  80 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  81 ‚îÇ ## Intended Behavior                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  82 ‚îÇ Description of what should happen or what the desired outcome is. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  83 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  84 ‚îÇ ## Proposed Solution                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  85 ‚îÇ Initial solution approach with implementation details. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  86 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  87 ‚îÇ ## Alternatives                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  88 ‚îÇ Alternative solutions proposed by:          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  89 ‚îÇ - Author                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  90 ‚îÇ - User                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  91 ‚îÇ - Other contributors                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  92 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  93 ‚îÇ ## Related Tools/Scripts                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  94 ‚îÇ Implementation tools, scripts, or dependencies that determine the solution space. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  95 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  96 ‚îÇ ## Modification History                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  97 ‚îÇ - {Date}: {Brief description of changes made} ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  98 ‚îÇ ```                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  99 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 100 ‚îÇ ### Issue Lifecycle                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 101 ‚îÇ                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 102 ‚îÇ 1. **Creation**: Create new `.issue` file with sequential ID ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 103 ‚îÇ 2. **Modification**: Add modification date and description to the end when changed ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 104 ‚îÇ 3. **Completion**: Move to `/issues/completed/` when resolved ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 105 ‚îÇ 4. **Review**: Regular review of open issues for priority and relevance ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îÇ   1 ‚îÇ # Assets Directory Structure               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   2 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   3 ‚îÇ This directory contains all Unity assets for the Preschool Ascension project. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   4 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   5 ‚îÇ ## Directory Organization                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   6 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   7 ‚îÇ ### Scripts/                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   8 ‚îÇ - **Player/**: Player controller, movement, interaction systems ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   9 ‚îÇ - **Environment/**: Preschool layout, physics materials, interactive objects ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  10 ‚îÇ - **LLM/**: Ollama integration, NPC AI, conversation systems ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  11 ‚îÇ - **UI/**: User interface, menus, HUD elements ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  12 ‚îÇ - **Core/**: Game architecture, managers, core systems ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ - **Utils/**: Utility functions, helpers, extensions ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  14 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ ### Scenes/                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  16 ‚îÇ - Unity scene files (.unity)               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  17 ‚îÇ - Organized by areas: Preschool, Basement, Outdoor areas ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  18 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  19 ‚îÇ ### Materials/                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  20 ‚îÇ - Physics materials for surfaces (cushions, floors, etc.) ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  21 ‚îÇ - Visual materials and shaders             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  22 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  23 ‚îÇ ### Textures/                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ - Image assets for materials               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ - UI elements and sprites                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ ### Models/                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ - 3D models for environment and props      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ - Character models and animations          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  30 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ ### Audio/                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ - Sound effects and background music       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ - Voice clips and ambient sounds           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  34 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ ### Prefabs/                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  36 ‚îÇ - Reusable game objects                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  37 ‚îÇ - Modular room components                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  38 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  39 ‚îÇ ### Animations/                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  40 ‚îÇ - Character animations                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  41 ‚îÇ - Environmental animations                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  42 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  43 ‚îÇ ### Resources/                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  44 ‚îÇ - Assets loaded at runtime                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  45 ‚îÇ - Configuration files                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  46 ‚îÇ - Data files                               ‚îÇ

‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ Written File: README.md (1324 bytes, 52 lines) ‚îÇ
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
‚îÇ   1 ‚îÇ # External Libraries                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   2 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   3 ‚îÇ This directory contains all external dependencies compiled from source. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   4 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   5 ‚îÇ ## Structure                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   6 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   7 ‚îÇ All libraries are built locally into this directory to avoid package manager dependencies. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   8 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   9 ‚îÇ ### Ollama Integration                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  10 ‚îÇ - Ollama will be compiled and installed here ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  11 ‚îÇ - Models and configurations stored separately (not in git) ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  12 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ ### Build Scripts                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  14 ‚îÇ - Located in `/build-scripts/` subdirectory ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ - Automated compilation scripts for all dependencies ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  16 ‚îÇ - Platform-specific build instructions     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  17 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  18 ‚îÇ ## Build Requirements                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  19 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  20 ‚îÇ Only basic compilation tools should be required: ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  21 ‚îÇ - GCC/Clang compiler                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  22 ‚îÇ - Make                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  23 ‚îÇ - Git (for fetching sources)               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ - Standard Linux development tools         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ No package managers or external installations required beyond basic system tools. ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ ## Usage                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  30 ‚îÇ 1. Check system dependencies:              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ ```bash                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ cd external-libraries/build-scripts        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ ./check-dependencies.sh                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  34 ‚îÇ ```                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  36 ‚îÇ 2. Build all dependencies:                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  37 ‚îÇ ```bash                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  38 ‚îÇ ./build-all.sh                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  39 ‚îÇ ```                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  40 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  41 ‚îÇ 3. Individual builds:                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  42 ‚îÇ ```bash                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  43 ‚îÇ ./build-ollama.sh          # Build Ollama LLM ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  44 ‚îÇ ./build-unity-native.sh    # Build Unity integration libraries ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  45 ‚îÇ ```                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  46 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  47 ‚îÇ ## Built Artifacts                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  48 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  49 ‚îÇ - **bin/ollama**: Ollama executable for LLM functionality ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  50 ‚îÇ - **lib/libollama_unity_bridge.so**: Native library for Unity-Ollama communication ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  51 ‚îÇ - **include/**: Header files for native integrations ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  52 ‚îÇ                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  53 ‚îÇ Built libraries are ignored by git but build scripts are tracked. ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  20 ‚îÇ if [ ! -d "$SRC_DIR/ollama" ]; then              ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  23 ‚îÇ else                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ     echo "Updating Ollama repository..."         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ     cd "$SRC_DIR/ollama"                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ     git fetch origin                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ fi                                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ cd "$SRC_DIR/ollama"                             ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ # Build Ollama                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ echo "Compiling Ollama..."                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  34 ‚îÇ go build -o "$BIN_DIR/ollama" .                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  62 ‚îÇ };                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  63 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  64 ‚îÇ static size_t WriteMemoryCallback(void *contents, size_t size, size_t nmemb, void *userp) { ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  65 ‚îÇ     size_t realsize = size * nmemb;                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  66 ‚îÇ     struct MemoryStruct *mem = (struct MemoryStruct *)userp; ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  67 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  68 ‚îÇ     char *ptr = realloc(mem->memory, mem->size + realsize + 1); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  69 ‚îÇ     if (!ptr) {                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  70 ‚îÇ         printf("Not enough memory (realloc returned NULL)\n"); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  71 ‚îÇ         return 0;                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  72 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  73 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  74 ‚îÇ     mem->memory = ptr;                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  75 ‚îÇ     memcpy(&(mem->memory[mem->size]), contents, realsize); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  76 ‚îÇ     mem->size += realsize;                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  77 ‚îÇ     mem->memory[mem->size] = 0;                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  78 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  79 ‚îÇ     return realsize;                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  80 ‚îÇ }                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  81 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  82 ‚îÇ int ollama_init(const char* url) {                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  83 ‚îÇ     curl_global_init(CURL_GLOBAL_DEFAULT);              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  84 ‚îÇ     curl = curl_easy_init();                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  85 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  86 ‚îÇ     if (curl && url) {                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  87 ‚îÇ         server_url = strdup(url);                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  88 ‚îÇ         return 1;                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  89 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  90 ‚îÇ     return 0;                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  91 ‚îÇ }                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  92 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  93 ‚îÇ char* ollama_chat(const char* prompt, const char* model) { ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  94 ‚îÇ     if (!curl || !prompt || !model) return NULL;        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  95 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  96 ‚îÇ     struct MemoryStruct chunk;                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  97 ‚îÇ     chunk.memory = malloc(1);                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  98 ‚îÇ     chunk.size = 0;                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  99 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 100 ‚îÇ     // Create JSON payload                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 101 ‚îÇ     char *json_data = malloc(strlen(prompt) + strlen(model) + 256); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 102 ‚îÇ     sprintf(json_data, "{\"model\":\"%s\",\"prompt\":\"%s\",\"stream\":false}", model, prompt); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 103 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 104 ‚îÇ     curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_URL, server_url);    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 105 ‚îÇ     curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_POSTFIELDS, json_data); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 106 ‚îÇ     curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_WRITEFUNCTION, WriteMemoryCallback); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 107 ‚îÇ     curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_WRITEDATA, (void *)&chunk); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 108 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 109 ‚îÇ     struct curl_slist *headers = NULL;                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 110 ‚îÇ     headers = curl_slist_append(headers, "Content-Type: application/json"); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 111 ‚îÇ     curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_HTTPHEADER, headers); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 112 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 113 ‚îÇ     CURLcode res = curl_easy_perform(curl);             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 114 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 115 ‚îÇ     free(json_data);                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 116 ‚îÇ     curl_slist_free_all(headers);                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 117 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 118 ‚îÇ     if (res != CURLE_OK) {                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 119 ‚îÇ         free(chunk.memory);                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 120 ‚îÇ         return NULL;                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 121 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 122 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 123 ‚îÇ     return chunk.memory;                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 124 ‚îÇ }                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 125 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 126 ‚îÇ void ollama_cleanup() {                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 127 ‚îÇ     if (curl) {                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 128 ‚îÇ         curl_easy_cleanup(curl);                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 129 ‚îÇ         curl = NULL;                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 130 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 131 ‚îÇ     if (server_url) {                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 132 ‚îÇ         free(server_url);                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 133 ‚îÇ         server_url = NULL;                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 134 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 135 ‚îÇ     curl_global_cleanup();                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 136 ‚îÇ }                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 137 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 138 ‚îÇ void ollama_free_response(char* response) {             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 139 ‚îÇ     if (response) {                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 140 ‚îÇ         free(response);                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 141 ‚îÇ     }                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 142 ‚îÇ }                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 143 ‚îÇ EOF                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 144 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 145 ‚îÇ # Copy header to include directory                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 146 ‚îÇ cp "$SRC_DIR/ollama_unity_bridge.h" "$INCLUDE_DIR/"     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 147 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 148 ‚îÇ # Compile the library                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 149 ‚îÇ echo "Compiling Ollama-Unity bridge library..."         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 150 ‚îÇ gcc -shared -fPIC -o "$LIB_DIR/libollama_unity_bridge.so" "$SRC_DIR/ollama_unity_bridge.c" -lcurl ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 151 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 152 ‚îÇ # Verify build                                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 153 ‚îÇ if [ -f "$LIB_DIR/libollama_unity_bridge.so" ]; then    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 154 ‚îÇ     echo "Unity bridge library built successfully: $LIB_DIR/libollama_unity_bridge.so" ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 155 ‚îÇ else                                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 156 ‚îÇ     echo "ERROR: Unity bridge library build failed"     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 157 ‚îÇ     exit 1                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 158 ‚îÇ fi                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 159 ‚îÇ                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 160 ‚îÇ echo "Unity native libraries build complete!"           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 161 ‚îÇ # }}}                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îÇ  13 ‚îÇ         MISSING_DEPS+=("$1")                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  14 ‚îÇ         echo "‚ùå $1 not found"                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  15 ‚îÇ     else                                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  16 ‚îÇ         echo "‚úÖ $1 found"                              ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  18 ‚îÇ }                                                      ‚îÇ

‚îÇ 146 ‚îÇ         {                                        ‚îÇ

‚îÇ 150 ‚îÇ                     if (mainMenuCanvas != null) mainMenuCanvas.gameObject.SetActive(true); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 151 ‚îÇ                     if (gameUICanvas != null) gameUICanvas.gameObject.SetActive(false); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 152 ‚îÇ                     break;                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 153 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 154 ‚îÇ                 case GameState.Playing:          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 155 ‚îÇ                     if (mainMenuCanvas != null) mainMenuCanvas.gameObject.SetActive(false); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 156 ‚îÇ                     if (gameUICanvas != null) gameUICanvas.gameObject.SetActive(true); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 157 ‚îÇ                     break;                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 158 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 159 ‚îÇ                 case GameState.Paused:           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 160 ‚îÇ                     // UI handled by pause menu specifically ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 161 ‚îÇ                     break;                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 162 ‚îÇ             }                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 163 ‚îÇ         }                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 164 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 165 ‚îÇ         private void Update()                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 166 ‚îÇ         {                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 167 ‚îÇ             // Handle escape key for pause/menu  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 168 ‚îÇ             if (Input.GetKeyDown(KeyCode.Escape)) ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 169 ‚îÇ             {                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 170 ‚îÇ                 if (isGameStarted)               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 171 ‚îÇ                 {                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 172 ‚îÇ                     TogglePause();               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 173 ‚îÇ                 }                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 174 ‚îÇ             }                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 175 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 176 ‚îÇ             // Debug key to reload config        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 177 ‚îÇ             if (Input.GetKeyDown(KeyCode.F5) && GameConfig.Instance.enableDebugMode) ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 178 ‚îÇ             {                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 179 ‚îÇ                 Debug.Log("Reloading configuration..."); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 180 ‚îÇ                 configManager?.LoadConfiguration(); ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 181 ‚îÇ             }                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 182 ‚îÇ         }                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 183 ‚îÇ                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 184 ‚îÇ         private void OnApplicationPause(bool pauseStatus) ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 185 ‚îÇ         {                                        ‚îÇ

‚îÇ 187 ‚îÇ             {                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 188 ‚îÇ                 SetPause(true);                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 189 ‚îÇ             }                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 190 ‚îÇ         }                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ 191 ‚îÇ     }                                            ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  24 ‚îÇ         [Header("Ground Check")]                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  25 ‚îÇ         [SerializeField] private LayerMask groundMask = 1;  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  26 ‚îÇ                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  27 ‚îÇ         private CharacterController controller;             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  28 ‚îÇ         private Vector3 velocity;                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  29 ‚îÇ         private bool isGrounded;                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  30 ‚îÇ         private float cameraRotationX = 0f;                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  31 ‚îÇ                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  32 ‚îÇ         private void Start()                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  33 ‚îÇ         {                                                   ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  35 ‚îÇ                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  36 ‚îÇ             // Lock cursor for FPS controls                 ‚îÇ
